THE PILLARS OF THE SKY

Dave Morris

Your Vulcanverse Adventure Starts Here

Vulcanverse is an open-world solo role-playing game. You can play the books in any order, starting anywhere you like, moving to other books whenever you travel to the region they cover. Instead of a single storyline, there are virtually unlimited adventures.

To play all you need is two dice, an eraser and a pencil. You only need one book to start, but by collecting other books in the series you can explore more of the Vulcanverse.

If you have already adventured using other books in the series, you will know your entry point into this book. Turn to that section now.

If this is your first Vulcanverse book, read the rest of the rules before starting at section **1**. You will keep the same adventuring persona throughout the books - starting out as a novice but gradually gaining in power, wealth and experience throughout the series.

**ADVENTURE SHEET**

The Adventure Sheet lists everything you'll need to keep track of while playing. Don't fill it in yet. That will happen as you begin your adventure.

**Attributes**

You have four attributes which typically range from -1 to +2 as you're starting out. You will discover your attribute scores as you play. They are:

Charm: Your understanding of people and their motives.

Grace: How agile, supple and quick you are.

Ingenuity: Cunning and reasoning, and your ability to think on your feet.

Strength: Physical might and endurance.

The maximum possible innate score in an attribute is +5. If you are already at maximum and are told to add to your score, it has no effect.

**Items that augment attributes**

There are items you can acquire during your adventure that boost your attributes while you have them. These are:

Charm: **laurel wreath** (+1) and **golden lyre** (+2)

Grace: **recurve bow** (+1) and **winged sandals** (+2)

Ingenuity: **hornbook** (+1) and **abacus** (+2)

Strength: **hardwood club** (+1) and **iron spear** (+2)

You can only use the bonus from one such item at a time. So if you had a **laurel wreath** that gives Charm +1 and a **golden lyre** that gives Charm +2, you'd only get the Charm bonus from the latter. Similarly, two **laurel wreaths** still only give you a +1.

An item can augment your attribute score above the innate limit of +5. If you have a Strength score of +5 and you possess an **iron spear**, your total Strength bonus when making a roll counts as +7.

**Making an Attribute Roll**

Attribute rolls are made to see if you succeed at a task. These are rolls of two dice with a difficulty that you must equal or beat to succeed.

For instance, you might be told: 'Make a Strength roll at difficulty 7'. You roll two dice, add your Strength score (including the modifiers for any one possession that boosts Strength) and to succeed you need to get 7 or more.

_Example: You are at the bottom of a cliff. To climb it you need to make a Grace roll at difficulty 5. You roll two dice and score 4. Your Grace attribute is -1 but luckily you have_ **_winged sandals_** _which give a +2 Grace bonus, so your modified Grace is +1, which is just enough to make the roll a success._

A roll of double 6 ('boxcars') is always a success regardless of difficulty. A roll of double 1 ('snake eyes') is always a failure regardless of modifiers.

**WOUNDS**

The Adventure Sheet has a box labelled Wound. This is unticked at the start of the adventure. From time to time you may be asked to put a tick in it. You only have one Wound tick at a time; if you're asked to tick the box when it is already ticked, you don't add another.

While the Wound box is ticked you have injuries, and these will cause you to deduct 1 from any attribute roll until the box is unticked.

**SCARS**

You begin with no scars, but may acquire them from lasting injuries or from returning from the afterlife. Scars are a mixed blessing. Many people will shun you because of them, but others will admire or fear you more.

**POSSESSIONS**

Possessions are always marked in bold text, like this: **iron spear**. If you come across an item marked like this you can pick it up and add it to your list of possessions.

You can carry up to twenty possessions at a time. If you come across an item you want when already at your limit, you'll have to discard something to make room. There are places in the Vulcanverse where you can leave possessions and come back for them later.

**MONEY**

You can carry any sum of money (measured in a currency called pyr). You'll discover as you play whether you have any money to start off with.

**GLORY**

Glory starts at 0 but will grow as you perform deeds that increase your renown. With high Glory you will be recognized as a hero and given more respect by those you meet.

**CODEWORDS**

There is a list of codewords. Sometimes you will be told you have acquired a codeword. When this happens, put a tick in the box next to that codeword. If you later lose the codeword, erase the tick.

The codewords are arranged alphabetically for each book in the series. In this book, for example, all codewords begin with Q. This makes it easy to check if you picked up a codeword from a book you played previously. For instance, you might be asked if you have picked up a codeword in a book you have already adventured in. The letter of that codeword will tell you which book to check (eg if it begins with N, it is from Book 1: _The Houses of the Dead_).

**TITLES**

Titles record the achievements you have earned, marking you as the champion of a city, protector of a temple, admiral of a fleet, or even a monarch. You will be told when you acquire a title.

**BLESSINGS**

If you fail an attribute roll, you can use up a blessing to roll the dice again. You can only do that once per roll, so you cannot use a second blessing to get another reroll if the first one fails.

You can have up to three blessings at a time. You start the adventure with no blessings. Usually the place to get blessings is at a shrine or temple, but you may find other opportunities to acquire them.

**COMPANION**

As you travel the Vulcanverse, you will meet some people who are willing to journey with you. You can have one companion at a time. When you pick up a new companion you must remove your current companion, if any, from the Companion box. You can also part company with a companion at any time just by deleting their name from the box. You do not have a companion at the start of the adventure.

**CURRENT LOCATION**

You'll use the Current Location box from time to time to keep track of where you are. You will be told when to use it. Whenever you are told to record an entry number in your Current Location box, first delete any number that was already there.

**NOTES**

Use the Notes box on your Adventure Sheet to keep a record of quests, clues or other things you need to remember.

That's all you need to know to get started on your adventure. Now turn to [**1**](#HeadingNum1)**.**

#### 1

In your waking moments you rarely think of your early life. The world is harsh, drawing a stark line between the quick and the dead, and so there is little time for idle reverie.

But when you sleep and your soul becomes unpinned from your body, time is a river that can flow both ways. Sometimes you see yourself then as an infant, standing on the hard-packed floor of your home as various uncles and aunts come with gifts for your birthday.

There is a man whose face is twisted by a scar that runs across his right eye, a sightless milky orb. He holds out a hand from which an old sword-cut sheared several fingers. Your uncle Nicomachus.

'No, little one, come to me,' calls your aunt Terpe from across the room, singing a merry song that makes you laugh in delight.

Your uncle Sophos has a gift for you. 'See these pictures of distant lands,' he says, holding up a book whose coloured pictures blaze as if with inner light. 'When you are a bit older you will read the words that describe these lands and travel there in your imagination.'

In the doorway waits your aunt Eremia. She never joins the throng at the hearth, always has one foot outside. 'Imagination's a fine thing. Better still to travel there in person.'

It is as though this moment has happened already. The four wait, and then you go to one of them. But which?

Scary uncle Nicomachus goto [**557**](#HeadingNum557)

Friendly aunt Terpe goto [**131**](#HeadingNum131)

Clever uncle Sophos goto [**663**](#HeadingNum663)

Restless aunt Eremia goto [**102**](#HeadingNum102)

#### 2

If Apollo is your god and you do not have the title **Unfriended by Apollo** then blessings cost 10 pyr each; otherwise they cost 35 pyr.

You can have a maximum of three blessings at a time. Each blessing can be used to reroll a failed attribute check (Charm, Grace, Ingenuity or Strength) but only once in any given situation - so if you fail the reroll, you can't spend another blessing to try again.

goto [**871**](#HeadingNum871)

#### 3

The building has no walls, being open on all sides with only marble pillars surrounding the interior. Even so, as you climb the steps and go inside the wind perceptibly drops.

A spring gushes from the far side of the temple, cascading down in a waterfall of sun-fractured droplets that forms the river that descends from here to the central plateau of Boreas.

Make an offering goto [**636**](#HeadingNum636)

Or descend the mountain:

'That's still my grain, you know,' snaps Echetus.

'Master Palanor told us to weigh it and give you a receipt,' says one of the slaves. 'If we just leave it on the floor the mice will have it.'

#### 7

You make as if to circle around looking for an opening, only to dart forward without warning and take a slashing cut as you run past him.

The tactic catches him by surprise and his sword comes up too slow to block yours. You turn to see blood flowing down his arm from a deep gash.

Now goto [**891**](#HeadingNum891) and tick one of the boxes there before reading on.

#### 8

The President of the High Council is a title that rotates each week. At the moment it is held by a small boy with a tuft of hair that sticks up at the back. Where you come from, if such a stripling spoke up among his elders he'd be spanked and sent outside to play, but here the whole assembly turns to hear him with respect.

'We need an army that can be summoned when needed,' he says. 'And it must be an army that we don't have to feed, because we have only enough to sustain our people. So the answer is to obtain the teeth of a dragon so that we can call on the Sown Men.'

Hand over **dragon's teeth** (if you have them) goto [**137**](#HeadingNum137)

Leave the council chamber goto [**566**](#HeadingNum566)

#### 10

'You will be rewarded richly for this,' says the King. He leads you to a tower of the palace that juts out over the canyon. Wind keens around it, causing a whistling through the high windows that is like the incessant scrape of chalk on slate.

In the highest chamber is a harp covered with ancient runes. Next to it, on the floor, is a sack of black leather. You look out of the window. There is a sheer drop that corkscrews down past long stretches of rock and disappears in the roiling clouds far, far below.

'I had this tower built as a place I could withdraw to and reflect on matters of state,' explains King Chalybos, 'but it is impossible to concentrate on anything while the wind keeps shrieking outside. With that harp, a skilful player can quieten the winds and entice them into this bag, whose string bears the glyph of the god Aiolos.'

'With respect, Your Majesty, you seem to be presenting me with a task rather than a gift.'

He snorts. 'It is both. If you succeed you get to keep the bag.'

You put your fingers on the harp strings and start to play.

If you have the **Orphean nail** goto [**675**](#HeadingNum675) and tick the box

Otherwise goto [**867**](#HeadingNum867)

#### 11

The fog billows through the gullies so thickly that you have to pick your way carefully among the rocks. From all around comes the trickling of water and the sound of a low, animal wailing. Creeping forward, you see a woman crouched on the ground. Her hair hangs around her and shelters a bundle she's cradling in her arms.

She looks up - not at you, but straight through you. Her face is paste-grey and her eyes are turned up in her head so that only the whites show. One side of her head is a broken mess of clotted black blood and tangled hair.

'I didn't know,' she moans. 'I thought it was safe. He tumbled in. Fell in the pot. It gave way. I didn't know it was loose.'

She holds up the bundle and you catch a glimpse of a tiny scarred face and burnt skin. Then the fog rolls across and she goes out like a candle flame.

If Loutro or Polymnia is here goto [**1030**](#HeadingNum1030)

Otherwise return to the road (goto [**141**](#HeadingNum141)) or continue to the end of the peninsula (goto [**113**](#HeadingNum113)).

Where are you bound?

#### 13

A few drops of the cockatrice's blood are enough to counteract the poison. Their breathing becomes deeper and regular. The children are first to wake, opening their eyes and yawning as if waking only from a long sleep and not a coma that took them to the brink of death.

The woodcutter and his wife sit up. 'Vrumino?' he says to the white-pelted minotaur.

'Stranger bring antidote,' rumbles Vrumino, pointing to you.

'Then we owe you our lives,' the wife says. goto [**340**](#HeadingNum340)

#### 14

The shepherd is sceptical about your plan but goes along with it as he hasn't got a better idea.

'Just to be clear,' he says, 'you're going to disguise yourself as a sheep?'

'Why not? It worked for Odysseus.'

'Cyclopes aren't as smart and wily as an old wolf. He'll smell you.'

'I'll stay downwind. And I'll be wearing a real sheepskin.'

He gives you a **sheepskin**; add it to your possessions. With it draped across your back, you kneel all night on the hillside. In the morning you are cold and cramped, and there has been no sign of the wolf.

'I said it wouldn't work,' sighs the shepherd. 'No, keep the sheepskin. You tried, after all, and I wouldn't want it said that Lycastus the shepherd lacks gratitude.'

goto [**964**](#HeadingNum964)

#### 15

Your attack scythes down, forcing him to parry desperately as you try to use main force to batter him down under a series of rapid blows.

Try a Strength roll at difficulty 11.

Success goto [**891**](#HeadingNum891) and tick one of the boxes there before reading on.

Failure goto [**947**](#HeadingNum947)

#### 16

'Go you to the peak of Mt Nysa, in the south of this realm,' says the ice nymph. 'There you will meet my cousin, one of the mountain nymphs, and if you offer her a suitable libation she may reward you with the means to calm the savage winds.'

'What libation, O goddess?'

'She nurtured the god Dionysos. That should give you some idea.'

You return to the shore goto [**848**](#HeadingNum848)

#### 17

He is propped against the tree. You know he's dead from the frost on his blue lips. When you swing him off the branches, his body slumps to the ground. His gullet has been torn right out, the blood cold and black as tar against the gaping hole in his throat and chest.

What kind of tiger is smart enough to drape a victim's corpse against a tree like that? Bait for a trap. And you walked straight into it.

There's a roar that makes your muscles go weak. Spinning around, you see a blur of white fur, glistening yellow talons, scythe-like fangs and amber-gold eyes that burn with a deathly feral fire.

goto [**1045**](#HeadingNum1045)

#### 18

A big man with a bushy black beard goes by at a sturdy pace, does a double take as he glances across at you, and comes back with a fierce look in his eye. You are thinking of reaching for a weapon to defend yourself when he grabs your hand and starts pumping it vigorously.

'I thought it was you!'

'I'm sorry, I don't - '

'No, no. Of course,' he booms heartily. 'You wouldn't remember me, but I was on the promontory down in Notus when you fixed the lighthouse. What a godsend to us sailors that's been. No longer have to shiver in our boots every time we tack around the rocks on that bit of coast.'

'I'm glad to hear it's still working.'

He reaches into his pack. 'Look here, I hope you won't be offended if I give you something. Token of gratitude, call it.'

He presses a **shaving mirror** into your hand. Add it to your possessions. Suddenly embarrassed, he mumbles a farewell and hurries off.

goto [**927**](#HeadingNum927)

#### 19

'Sandalwood,' she says. 'It's related to mistletoe, though you'd hardly know from that rich fragrance.'

You put your nose to the box and sniff. The warm spicy aroma evokes far-off ports where lateen-rigged ships bob at anchor.

'Bees love sandalwood,' says Polymnia. 'They seem to find the smell comforting.'

'Thanks. I'll add that to the other thousand useless facts you've stuffed in my head.'

Go north goto [**200**](#HeadingNum200)

Go south goto [**330**](#HeadingNum330)

#### 20

You drive the attackers off, but not without taking a few bruises. Tick the Wound box on your Adventure Sheet if it was not ticked already.

Also roll one die, and if you get 5 or 6 then one of them managed to grab your purse in the scuffle and you have lost all your money.

goto [**263**](#HeadingNum263)

#### 21

The crate is carried down through the streets and loaded onto a ship. After a few hours there's a cry of 'cast off!' You hear the lapping of the waves, the creak of timbers, the steady drumbeat that sets the pull of the oars.

A crowbar is driven into the lid, snapping the crate open. Rough hands reach in and drag you out, throwing you to the deck in front of a swaggering captain.

'Well, well. An unexpected passenger.'

'What gave me away?'

He gives a great shout of laughter. 'Chintz, of all things. You ordered a divan with a pattern of tulips. The lady of the house hates tulips, so naturally the carpenter queried the order - and here you are.'

You get to your feet. There's no sign of land, just the grey swell of the sea in all directions. 'And where is here?'

The captain gestures, and two crewmen pull you to an oar where you are chained among the other slaves. 'This metre of bench is your whole world from now on,' says the captain. 'You weren't such a hotshot as a scribe, so we'll see how you do as a galley slave. Row for all your worth and maybe you'll even develop a set of muscles.'

He turns away, losing interest in you. Now you are just one of dozens of weary, sweat-soaked slaves who must pull at the oars or else feel the sting of the slave-master's whip.

If you have the codeword **_Quake_** goto [**561**](#HeadingNum561)

If not but you have **_Pumped_** goto [**326**](#HeadingNum326)

Otherwise goto [**740**](#HeadingNum740)

#### 22

The lock on the main warehouse door and Echetus's own padlock on the storeroom both seem secure.

'And only you had the key to this padlock?' you ask him. 'Palanor didn't find that suspicious?'

'That's how we always do business,' says Echetus. 'Palanor stores people's goods here and arranges carts for shipments. He has the key to the warehouse, and each merchant has the key to his own storeroom. The foolproof security system.'

'Until now.'

Look at the jars goto [**747**](#HeadingNum747)

Interrogate Echetus goto [**764**](#HeadingNum764)

#### 23

A crackling fire brings you to your senses. There's a bandage round your head and the sharp pain in your side tells you you've cracked a few ribs.

'Awake, are you? Expect you're hungry.'

You ease yourself up on one elbow. You're in a small hut. Animal hides are pinned to the walls. The trapper looks up from the fire where a pot of stew is bubbling away.

'How did I get here?'

'Found you lying in the snow. Fell out of a tree, is my guess. Were you after that?' He points the ladle at a cat's skin. 'Take it if you want. Souvenir, like. The meat is all I care about.'

He hands you a bowl of stew. If you want the **catskin**, add it to your possessions. When you are ready to resume your journey goto [**876**](#HeadingNum876)

#### 24

The tricky bit will be reaching out to take the ring while continuing to play the flute one-handed.

Try a Grace or Charm roll at difficulty 14. (It's your choice as to which and reflects whether you are concentrating on the manual dexterity of playing or the quality of the music.)

Success goto [**832**](#HeadingNum832)

Failure goto [**622**](#HeadingNum622)

#### 25

Even as you throw yourself forward, the enemy commander drives his sword-point straight towards you. Each of you twists to the side, trying to avoid your opponent's attack without losing the opportunity to inflict a hit.

Make a Grace roll at difficulty 8 and, if you fail, his sword scores you across the chest and you must put a tick in the Wound box if it was not ticked already.

Then goto [**308**](#HeadingNum308)

#### 26

A group of children follow you along the street chanting a mocking rhyme about foreigners.

'Hoy, you kids!' yells a street-sweeper. 'Get away.'

'Thank you,' you say to him as the children scowl and turn away.

He doesn't look at you and doesn't even seem to be listening. Still addressing the children, he says, 'You can catch all sorts of diseases from foreigners, remember that!'

goto [**624**](#HeadingNum624)

#### 27

The wooden supports can no longer take the strain. They splinter like kindling and the roof of the shaft lurches down, dislodging a cascade of rocks and dust that knocks you to the ground. Tick the Wound box on your sheet if it was not ticked already.

You raise your head and look around. You must have blacked out. There's just a narrow slit of daylight at the entrance. You couldn't possibly squeeze through, even if you didn't have a beam pinning your legs. Clutching about in the dust-choked gloom, your fingers close on a **bucket of gypsum**. A fat lot of good that will do you, but add it to your possessions if you want.

If you have the codeword **_Quarter_** and this box [TICKBOX] is empty, tick it and goto [**117**](#HeadingNum117)

Otherwise goto [**943**](#HeadingNum943)

#### 28

The figure gives a high-pitched snort of thwarted rage and shrinks like a deflated balloon. It's not your god at all, just a stunted little creature with a face like a scrunched-up glove holding a droopy carrot.

'A kobalos!' gasps the mate. 'They're known for their shape-changing tricks.'

'Piss-pots,' says the creature, clambering up the rigging. 'Fart-bags. Bums with smelly boils on.'

'Charming little devil,' you remark to the mate. 'Somebody get a bow and shoot him.'

The kobalos spits with remarkable accuracy, hitting you right in the eye, and then lets go of the mast and is swept away on the raging wind.

You have lost all your blessings, if you had any. But is that because of the kobalos's curse, or because you showed a lack of faith in your deity? Even though it wasn't your deity, gods can be capricious like that.

'Look lively,' cries the steersman. 'We've reached the end of the vortex.'

You emerge back into normal reality to find yourselves in a massive open-roofed cavern or crater, kilometres across, which forms the edges of a lake or inland sea.

goto [**787**](#HeadingNum787)

Below their broad terraces, the city descends in tiers down to the slums that are lapped by water and perpetually cloaked in lake mist. Lead pipes wind down the cliff carrying effluent of the rich that seeps into the foundations of the poor.

#### 35

You leave a few moments of silence, then give vent to a piercingly loud squeal of pleasure. There's a satisfying bustling from outside the door as Fortunatus retreats in embarrassed confusion. You can hear him mumbling to himself as he hurries off downstairs.

Ransacking the room you find trinkets worth 90 pyr. Add it to your money. Thanks to the decorative trellis on the front of the house it's an easy climb down to the street, and you are soon clear of the gloom of the Great Sinkhole and out under the clean stars of the High Steppes.

goto [**140**](#HeadingNum140)

#### 39

Sharp beaks tear chunks out of you (tick the Wound box if you weren't already injured) but you manage to stay on the ledge and fight your way through to the nest. With one arm raised to fend off the hippogriffs' attacks, you snatch blindly at a few items scattered amid the twigs and grass that make up the nest. You get an **amulet against Alastor** and a **lava gem**. Add them to your possessions.

Attracted by the commotion, more hippogriffs are flying down to join the affray. You cast a quick glance out from the ledge and see a few narrow projections. If you time it just right, you could jump down from one to another and get to the bottom of the cliff in a few leaps. If you mistime it, you'll be a broken wreck on the rocks below.

Make a Grace roll at difficulty 11 to pull it off.

Like a mountain goat goto [**70**](#HeadingNum70)

Like a lead weight goto [**726**](#HeadingNum726)

#### 40

It is simple butchery, the work of a moment, and they lie together in final embrace as their lifeblood wells out to soak the mattress under them. Lose the codeword **_Quaff_**.

Now - escape. The window catch - stuck! With a wrench it shifts slightly, emitting a loud metallic rasp as it scrapes against the frame. You freeze, still holding the clasp.

Footsteps in the corridor outside. A discreet tap on the door, more terrifying for being hushed than if someone had begun pounding on it.

'Sir? Madam?'

It's the major-domo, Fortunatus.

Ignore him, just get the window open goto [**586**](#HeadingNum586)

Get him to go away goto [**697**](#HeadingNum697)

He'll have to die too goto [**492**](#HeadingNum492)

#### 42

'Mind if I get a piece of the action?' you ask, taking a seat at a table piled with coins and dice.

'You're a foreigner, I see,' says the man next to you, ' but no doubt your coins are as good as anyone's. It's five obols to throw - or five "purrs", I guess you outlanders would say.'

They roar with laughter at his attempt at copying your accent. If you have 5 pyr to stake on a throw goto [**625**](#HeadingNum625)

If not goto [**729**](#HeadingNum729)

#### 43

The wind rushes back, shrieking around the columns of the hypostyle hall and snatching at your clothes and hair. As you stagger in the gale, one of your belongings flies from your backpack and is carried away out of reach. Remove one attribute-boosting item from your possessions. The wind's order of preference is Strength, then Grace, then Ingenuity and finally Charm, and it will of course steal a +2 item in preference to a +1.

A particularly strong gust plucks you off your feet, carries you back to the entrance, and deposits you on the steps outside.

There is nothing you can achieve here so it's time to leave.

goto [**279**](#HeadingNum279)

#### 44

#### 47

As the ship moves out clear of the docks, you're aware of a tension in the air that is resolved by a shivering note that is almost too high to hear. At first you think it's just your imagination, but you notice the narrowed eyes and flaring nostrils of your fellow slaves.

The hateful drum-beat quickens. Ahead of the ship, the water begins to swirl around in a maelstrom of surging foam and writhing tendrils of fog. It deepens into a whirlpool that sucks at the ship. The prow lurches, tilts down, and you are plunging into a dark abyss that is like sailing between multiple waterfalls so huge that they blot out all daylight.

The ship is buffeted about, forcing the crew to cling to the rail. In gaps through the roaring torrent of water it's possible to glimpse uncanny vistas stretching at impossible angles. A light appears ahead, and then a gust of icy wind and you bob up like a cork onto a wide expanse of grey ocean. The maelstrom behind you subsides until the only motion is the rise and fall of the swell.

'What you all gawping at?' the oar master yells. 'Ain't you never gone through a sea gate before?'

#### 102

You take your aunt's hand and lead her out of the open doorway. The horizon seems to call to you. Across the fields and the vineyards, over the streams and forests, up into the blue hills and beyond. That is where your destiny will lead you. Without looking back you start to run, filled with the exhilaration of the world that is spread around you.

'Go, fierce one,' calls your aunt, her words almost lost in the wind. 'You'll never catch the Huntress till your dying day, but till then strive to keep her always in your sight.'

So, your god is Artemis. Write her name in the box on your Adventure Sheet and goto [**1019**](#HeadingNum1019)

#### 108

You brace yourself so it is over quick. One stroke. The flash of the axe, the spurt of red on the snow-crusted pine needles, the thud as the severed head rolls off the block. You carry it to a bucket and collect the blood, which you use to moisten the cracked lips of the four people indoors.

Minutes pass. Was the minotaur deluded? Did he die in vain?

'Hey!' The woodcutter's elder son is sitting up. He shakes his parents and his sister, whose breathing has become steady and regular. They open their eyes and stretch, weak with their long illness but no longer bearing the pallor of approaching death.

'Did you save our lives?' asks the woodcutter, getting shakily to his feet.

You nod. 'That's the good news. There's also some bad.'

#### 112

You could get to it along the shore and try climbing if you have a head for heights and a disdain for risk.

#### 117

You lie helpless for hours watching the thin trickle of daylight darken into night. Pain and thirst combine to make your sleep feverish, and a new dawn finds you too weak to move.

As you are composing yourself for death, heavy footsteps crunch across the gravel outside. Huge hands plant themselves around the snapped beam at the entrance. You hear an intake of breath into mighty lungs, then a bellow as the beam is lifted up. There's just enough room for you to crawl out to safety.

'Hurry,' says the minotaur, his voice full of strain.

'Can't move.'

'It's that or die.'

With the last of your strength you pull your legs free of the fallen joist and squirm out into the open air. The minotaur grunts and lets the beam fall back. A cloud of stone dust billows out around you both.

It's the minotaur you put the nose ring on. When you've both recovered your breath, you ask him about life among the bosgyns.

'It's not so bad. They talk absolute rubbish from dawn to dusk and then tell me I'm too thick to understand it, but they're decorative at least.'

'How did you know I was in trouble?'

'Just a hunch. Or maybe the gods put it into my head. Lucky for you either way. Anyway, I can't laze about. Got chores to do.'

He lumbers off. Where will you go now?

#### 138

#### 140

The Great Sinkhole is a vast crater in the centre of the high steppes. Here the four rivers that run from the mountains of the oreads spill down into its depths to fill the lake a hundred metres below. A shroud of fog seethes whitely over the lip of the sinkhole, formed by the relatively warmer water of the lake steaming up into the chill air that hangs here in permanent shadow under a grey sky.

All around the rim of the sinkhole, tunnelled into its walls and built out on jetties, is the grim citadel of the Gargareans. At the topmost level, around the sinkhole rim, are the palaces and townhouses of the most prosperous. Further down, sunk in the dripping murk that shades the streets in perpetual twilight, are the meaner dwellings: the taverns, the slave pits, the prison, the docks, and the tenements and slums where most Gargareans live out their lives in brooding hatred of all foreigners.

#### 169

Amid the jumble of dreams of your past, you have a fading image in which you were following somebody along a beach as the tide came in, each step harder to take as you waded through the surf.

That's easily explained by the salt smell on the breeze and the seagulls screeching overhead, circling white shapes in a sky of clear blue. The sound of singing is coming from a hall overlooking a picturesque harbour town. You must have arrived here late last night, thrown your pack down in the alley to serve as a pillow, and dropped off from sheer exhaustion.

Going to the front of the hall you see all the townsfolk crowding through the door. 'Ah, you're here for the contest,' says a fat motherly woman who is selling tickets.

'I don't know if I have enough...'

You are surprised to find a fistful of coins in your pocket. She takes them. 'Get these out of a shipwreck, did you?' she says laughing. 'Ancient, these are. Still, silver is silver. In you go.'

The hall is crowded to the rafters. Each contestant goes forward to a small wooden stage to sing, and they are greeted with a cacophony of whistles, clapping, shouts and laughter. Everybody seems to be having a whale of a time.

You find yourself being pushed towards the stage. 'But I don't know any songs,' you protest.

'Open your mouth,' says a voice in your ear. 'See what comes out.' You turn but there is no one there.

As you start to sing, the previously rowdy audience go silent. They listen raptly to your song, and the next minute they're stamping along and joining in. 'We have a winner!' shouts the master of ceremonies.

You are given a purse stuffed with coins. Gain 30 pyr. As well as that, you can't forget the sea shanty that seemed to come into your head from nowhere; get the codeword **_Quoit_**.

Leave the town goto [**200**](#HeadingNum200)

With a crack like eternity coming to an end, the ice gives way and you are sucked down into dense watery silence. The heat drains out of your body, yet strangely the sensation is of prickling warmth. You welcome the enfolding darkness, the comforting numbness, the chance to sleep deeply after many travails.

A light burns through the darkness. Loud, jangling sounds intrude on your repose. There's a stink of wet fur, hot meaty breath, damp clothing. You are vomiting water as something heavy and ungentle presses down on your back.

You open your eyes to find you've been dragged to the shore. You are face to face with a sabre-toothed creature whose amber eyes are smoking beacons of ageless intelligence. It yawns and flexes its claws, each bigger than any dagger. Then it turns and pads off into the snowstorm.

Numb with cold, you drag yourself to a thicket where you manage to gather a few scraps of wood. The wood is damp and you can't get it alight. Shivering uncontrollably, you give in again to the swamping darkness, but this time you wake wrapped in a woollen blanket beside a crackling fire.

The hunter looks at you. 'Went in the lake, did you? Not many live to tell about that.'

You open your mouth to relate everything that happened, and in that moment you realize that it was not one of those experiences of which you can ever speak.

goto [**629**](#HeadingNum629) and tick the box there before reading on.

#### 214

'Perhaps I can help.'

'Only if you have the means of conjuring up an army. Each year we are raided by our warlike neighbours. They covet our grain and fruit and livestock, but they don't bother to grow their own as they'd rather just steal what we have.'

It rolls over and beckons you. Not a spider, then. A hand. As your eyes adjust to the gloom, you see a figure lean forward. His face is thin and hard, a skull with layers of cobwebs across it. The hand and the rest of him too: just bones held together by spider-silk and creepers.

'I was once handsome and tall as you,' he says in a rustling voice. 'But the Fates are neither fond nor grudging of men. They took my youth, snuffed out my life when it had barely begun. They took no notice of my life, snipping the thread without thought. But I cannot let go of life, so here I stay as time picks at my bones.'

#### 261

You bring the boat as close to the pounding surf as you dare, then swim ashore and climb up to the coral basin on the headland. Cold and wet, you wait until the stars come out watery and shimmering across the sky. Judging it to be midnight, you stir the water in the coral basin. The whirlpool speeds up but also becomes more regular - a swirling purposeful current rather than a chaotic maelstrom. The centre of the whirlpool dips and an eldritch glow seeps up from fathomless distance.

You hurry back to the boat. 'Set the prow dead ahead. Take us straight in.'

'But, cap'n!'

'Trust me.'

Your boat is buffeted by the waves and lurches as she passes through the outer edge of the whirlpool. For a moment it seems as if you are tipping off the edge of the world, but gravity tilts with you and now you are being carried on by a smooth current towards the distant gleam ahead.

#### 266

Along with some other new slaves you are taken to a townhouse on the highest tier of the cliffside city, its roof almost level with the top of the sinkhole. You are herded around the back into a cellar room with a few dirty blankets strewn on the rough stone floor.

'Is one of these my bed?'

The major-domo, himself a slave but one with status and privileges, gives you a disdainful sidelong glance. 'You and the other menials will share these blankets. While one sleeps, another works.'

As you are being instructed in your duties, you catch sight of a slender woman with a lithe, coiled, restless, prowling walk, pacing around the slave quarters like a panther trapped in the confines of a too-small cage. Curls of dark wiry hair half-cover her face, giving her a drowsy look until you notice the smouldering madness in those heavy-lidded eyes.

'Penthé!' You seize her arm. After a moment she turns her face towards you but gives no sign of recognition. 'Don't you remember me? We met in Hades.'

'I know you,' she says in colourless tones.

'Didn't you have a companion?'

'They killed her.'

She pulls away from you and resumes her furious pacing. 'She has been like that since she was first brought here,' one of the kitchen slaves says. 'Some can't adjust to not having freedom.'

'Why should they?' you reply. 'I plan to escape at the first opportunity.'

'You know what they do to runaway slaves? You're better off accepting your lot.'

You're no longer listening to him, because you notice that the moment you spoke of escape, Penthé ceased her pacing and turned to stare across the room at you.

#### 269

Distantly below you see the icy light of Boreas, and against that are the shadows of towers and men, seen moving far-off but in sharp glittering focus, like figures in a desert mirage.

#### 281

After a few minutes an eerie mewling sound can be heard. Shambling out of the fog come three figures: the frightened child, the angry man, and the weeping woman.

And yet - now they are not gripped by overpowering passions, as they were before. They move like sleepwalkers to the side of the stone table and start lapping up the contents of the bowl.

'Your wife didn't mean to kill the baby,' you tell the man. 'She put it on a shelf that was loose and it fell into the fire.'

He stares at you dully, the mallet limp in his hands. Turning to the child, you say, 'It wasn't your fault. You couldn't know what would happen. Don't blame yourself.'

The child looks from you to its father, the look of guilt and worry fading to leave its features clear.

'And you had no way of knowing the shelf would give way,' you say to the wife. 'Accidents happen. It's a tragedy, but not one with a villain. All of you are victims, lashing out at yourselves and each other in your pain. But let go of that and you can go to your rest together.'

As you say that, the baby starts tugging at its mother's hair. She looks at it and smiles, and now the side of her head isn't caved-in and bloody. The man no longer has his hammer. He puts an arm around her, another round the child, and leads them off towards a light that shines through the fog.

You follow but they have vanished from the mortal world. You're about to turn back when you notice a coppery gleam among the rocks. Clearing away handfuls of moss you uncover the **greaves of the** **Lost Hero.** Add them to your possessions and then make your way back to the road.

#### 318

The surface of the glacier is as uneven as a storm-tossed sea frozen into sudden immobility. Gusts of chill air blow across it, but the labour of clambering over ridges and through dips in the ice keeps you warm.

Heated by the sun, the glacier has spawned a hundred little streams that run gurgling through the immensity of its bulk. From time to time there is an ominous crack and you stand stock-still, expecting the terrain to give way and plunge you down the mountainside. But it has endured millennia in darkness, against which a few days of sunshine makes little difference.

Through a bank of thick white fog you see a hut on a rock overlooking the glacier. Blocks of glistening ice are stacked up outside the door. Beyond the hut, a narrow track leads up among the rocks.

#### 328

'A donkey and a horse were on a journey with their master. "Oh, I can't go on," said the donkey, who was carrying everything. "This load is breaking my back. "I was a fool," thought the horse, "I wouldn't carry a light load, so now I have to carry the lot."'

Eso acts out all the parts brilliantly - the put-upon, bone-weary donkey, the disdain of the horse, the shock and regret as it realizes it's got to carry everything. Yet the effect is like a snack rather than a meal.

#### 372

#### 374

You crouch among the rocks near where the sheep graze. Night draws its cloak around the hills and a swollen white moon rises to bathe the landscape in a soft silvery light.

Close to midnight, a shape detaches itself from the shadows high up on the hillside and veers silently towards the dim white form of one of the sheep.

You're on your feet as the spear leaves your hand. It arcs across the space between you and buries itself in the wolf's side. Even now he makes almost no sound, just a frantic snapping of jaws as he works himself free and lopes off back up the hill.

Reminded of a note you once read in Hades, you narrow down the search to a particular part of the mountain slopes where the best trees grow for shipbuilding. After several days your persistence is rewarded by the discovery of a rope elevator suspended from the top of a sheer cliff.

#### 383

You stalk a herd of mammoths for several days, being careful to keep downwind and out of sight. Such huge creatures are easy to track, leaving heavy prints even in this frozen unyielding sward.

Shortly after dawn on the third day, you see them gathered around a frozen lake. Fog steams on the chill air, allowing you to creep quite close. The mammoths have broken the ice and the adults are gathering water in their trunks to warm it before passing it on to the calves.

Seeing them close up you are daunted at the prospect of tackling them. Even the young are as big as buffalos, and the adult males are craggy giants whose matted coats make them look like briar-covered cliffs. Most of the adults are female, but even they are terrifyingly huge.

You notice that one of the young mammoths, a half-grown male, has wandered inquisitively along the lake shore away from the others. A giant of a bull mammoth also stands aloof at a distance from the herd, apparently on guard against attackers.

'You hear a lot about the Amazons, not so much about the Halizons. Yet they used to share these steppes long ago.'

'Allies?'

'Constantly at war. Originally they were one tribe and they were ruled on alternate days by a king and a queen. Not a married couple, you understand - these two were of different royal lines, the Halizonian and the Amazonian dynasties. Anyway, an Amazonian princess called Lampeto decided she'd make a better ruler than her sister Marpesia, so she murdered her. When it came to light, the Halizonian monarch said that proved that women weren't fit to rule. And that's when the tribe split.'

'And all the women went off to found the Amazons?'

'Not all, but the women who stayed became subservient to their menfolk and are not allowed outside without a mask to hide their face, so lots of people think the Halizons are an all-male tribe the way the Amazons are all female.'

#### 445

After a few minutes, a small skiff returns through the whirlpool gate and its officer is brought to the flagship. He has a blood-soaked bandage tied around his head. 'The enemy is alerted,' he gasps. 'Our advance party is under heavy attack.'

You give the signal. 'All ships - sail into the whirlpool.'

It is like falling off the edge of the world. You see the fear in the mariners' faces, fear they do not allow themselves to stop and feel. Your vessels plunge into the maelstrom and you look back to see them sailing along the churning watery walls of a tunnel in space.

Another lurch as your pow bobs up onto the inland sea. The walls of the sinkhole surround you on all sides, but the wide expanse of water is easily big enough for a pitched naval battle. Lined up against you are the warships of the Gargarean fleet - those same ships that ransacked Iskandria, plundered her wealth, carried off her women, slaughtered her sons. And now you see the look on your sailors' faces. It is not fear now. It is eagerness to settle old scores.

#### 451

In the seraglio you are granted an audience with Princess Myrina, the latest in the female royal line. 'Of course,' she explains, 'these days it's only a courtesy title. The male royal line is the only one with authority among the Halizons since the days of my ancestor Princess Lampeto. She murdered her sister, and that gave the men a pretext for seizing power. They said that Lampeto's treachery showed that women couldn't be trusted to rule wisely.'

You smile. 'If one sociopath on the throne invalidated the whole concept of monarchy, there wouldn't be a single crowned ruler anywhere in the Vulcanverse.'

'If Lampeto could be redeemed, we could prove to the men that they were wrong to abandon the old ways. Men and women could be equals again.'

'Wasn't it centuries ago, though?' you say dubiously. 'Too late for redemption, surely?'

'Somebody would need to travel to Hades,' says Myrina, leaning forward and fixing you with an imploring gaze. 'There a demon tortures my ancestor's shade for her crime. But if she could be rescued, that would prove that the gods have forgiven her, and if the gods forgive her...'

'Then of course it would be sacrilege for the Halizonian men not to do so.' You nod. 'Just need somebody to go to Hades and get her, then.'

Myrina gives you a joyful grin. 'Thank you. And incidentally I think you should set out right away.'

#### 453

A memory comes to you. A dark alleyway, furtive voices, whispered secrets in the dead of night. 'Stir the basin counter-clockwise at midnight,' the traitor said. It's worth a try.

The daylight drains away and slowly the moon crawls into the sky, turning the violent crashing waves into luminous geysers of silver lava. A few stars struggle to be seen through the haze of spray.

At last, judging it to be midnight, you lean over the basin and stir. The water is icy cold. As you stir, you realize that counter-clockwise is also the direction of the whirlpool.

The current intensifies, yet at the same time seems to become more controlled. Instead of the chaos of clashing waves, there is now a purposeful current that grows faster and stronger, lowering the sea in the centre of the whirlpool into a funnel that descends into unknown depths. From far, far below you see a blue radiance. It is like looking along a tunnel into another region of the Vulcanverse. And do you see, far in the distance there, a skyline of buildings and moving figures..?

After a while the glow fades, the current eases and becomes choppy again, and all is as it was before. Except that now you know how to open a gateway through the sea - and you know how a huge war-fleet was able to sail from this small island to sack Iskandria and then vanish without trace. Get the codeword **_Quagmire_**.

'We've all done it.'

He laughs, half a sneer. 'You? Muscles like minnows, you've got.'

#### 487

You take a step forward in alarm. The minotaur plants a huge hand in front of you. 'Wait. Is good thing.'

The serpent fades into a greenish mist that seeps into the sick people's skin. Moments pass. A log cracks in the hearth, shooting cinders up the chimney. The door bangs in the wind.

The woodcutter gives a gasp and sits up. 'Water - '

The minotaur kneels at his side, offering him a drink. The wife and children stir, open their eyes, and sit up.

'A strange dream,' says the wife.

'I saw it too, Ma,' says the older child. 'A place of damp mist. People crying...'

'That was Hades you saw,' you tell them. 'But now you're back.'

#### 512

You carefully detach the fragile empty skin from the rocks, fill it with the bones, and bury it at the cave mouth. At least this way the satyr's spirit may be able to rest in peace.

As it is late, you make camp and watch the sky shade from purple to black. The stars are tiny crystals of light filling the cosmos. Lost in a sense of wonder, you give a start as a hoof steps beside you and a fine baritone voice says, 'Who do I thank for my resurrection?'

Jumping up, you see that the satyr has come back to life. The skin that was leathery and dry a few hours earlier is pliant and suffused with the bloom of healthy circulation. The loose bones are now reknit by sinew and muscle.

His face crinkles into a grin. 'It's so boring being dead. I'm Marsyas, by the way.'

He tells you his story. Having had the temerity to challenge the god Apollo to a musical contest, he stupidly won. Apollo peeled off his skin, scattered the bones, and pinned him up in this cave. The incessant tears of his sisters, the nymphs, fed the stream which has now dried up.

You spend a couple of days here with Marsyas and he teaches you how to hold an audience spellbound with music, song or simple speech. Get +1 Charm and acquire the title **Unfriended by Apollo**. Also remember to delete the **bag of bones** from your possessions.

#### 542

The ascent is arduous, consisting of narrow ledges over precipitous drops and crevices that you have to squeeze through to stay on the path.

#### 552

There's a long-handled hammer among a pile of tools in the corner of the warehouse. You pick it up, march outside to the cart, and take a swing at the nearest jar. With a crash it bursts apart. Grain spills out into the mud.

'You're crazy!' says Palanor, running over. 'Pisco, grab that hammer.'

Pisco steps forward, sees the look in your eyes and thinks better of it. They watch in horror as you smash another couple of jars.

'My friend,' says Echetus, 'this will do no good.'

The fourth jar breaks open, but this time it's not only grain that comes spilling out. Kicking and spluttering, a wiry little man tumbles onto the ground. He sits there blinking in the sunlight with a hollow straw clamped between his teeth.

You laugh. 'Bit big for a mouse, wouldn't you say?'

From the broken jar behind him, a stream of gems trickles out.

'My gems!' says Echetus. 'Who is this man?'

'The thief. One of them.' You haul back with the hammer, bash open another couple of jars, and here are three guilty-looking miscreants, each with a small pile of gems under him.

'How did they get in there?'

'They were there all along,' you tell him. 'They hid themselves inside three of the jars when you went off to get the gems. A layer of grain on top in case you checked, and those hollow straws to breathe through. Once the room was locked up, they emerged, tipped over three jars looking for the one with the gems, and broke one in the process. Once they had the gems, each took some and got back in their jar, burrowing down under a layer of grain as before. The idea was that you'd think the gems were gone for good, and you wouldn't much care about the grain that was left so - '

'You've got no proof I knew anything about it,' says Palanor hastily.

'Got Pisco here, though,' you say, grabbing the potter by the neck before he can slink away. 'He heard from the jeweller that Echetus had cashed in his money for gems, and when Echetus also bought a bunch of grain jars he put two and two together.'

Echetus summons the town guard and they escort Pisco and the three thieves to lockup. He turns a glowering look on Palanor. 'Maybe your accomplices will implicate you, maybe not. Time will tell.'

For recovering his gems, Echetus rewards you with 1000 pyr. Add it to your money, and also get +1 Glory. You bid him farewell and continue on your way.

'I've been saving up scraps of food,' she mutters as she hands you a fresh armful of laundry.

She nods.

You lean closer, anxious not to be overheard through the open kitchen door. 'What's the plan? We'll need warm clothing out on the steppes. Strong boots, too, not these flimsy sandals they gave us.'

'I've worked it all out,' she says in her husky voice that brooks no argument.

That night, as you crawl wearily to the blanket to sleep, your hand encounters a parcel of bread and dripping. Compared to the scraps you were given at supper it is a feast.

#### 582

Decide on your stake (between 1 and 10 pyr) which you put into the pot. Then roll the dice to see if you win or lose:

score 2-4 Get back three times your stake

score 5 Get back twice your stake

score 6-12 Lose your stake

So if for example you wagered 5 pyr and rolled a 4, you'd take back 15 pyr from the pot - a gain of 10 pyr on top of getting back your original stake.

goto [**1068**](#HeadingNum1068)

#### 598

The shouts of the triumphant mingle with the screams of the dying and the whimpers of the terrified. From all around comes the discordant music of battle: clanging swords, incessant drums, the hiss and thud of arrows, the crack of timbers. Flames lick around a forest of masts; smoke interlaces with the icy mist; the tang of fresh snapped wood combines with the stench of sweat and fear and spilled blood. Ships collide, prows splintering through hulls, grapples tearing into rigging. All is chaos and desperation, the very sustenance of Ares as he breathes and drinks the violent struggles of mortals.

#### 599

The other slaves follow your lead, snapping the oars and using the broken pieces as spears and bludgeons. The Gargarean crew fight fiercely, but they are overwhelmed by weight of numbers.

At sunset the sky is no redder than the blood-soaked planks of the ship. Glutted by slaughter, the now-free oarsmen raise the sail and tack the vessel along the coast.

There is a whimper from under one of the benches. The oar master is dragged out. He lies limp on the deck staring up at the angry faces of those he was accustomed to torment.

'Now you'll make me your slave,' he says, licking his lips nervously.

A man with long whip-scars across his neck and shoulders raises a belaying pin. 'No,' he growls. 'After what I've gone through I'll never enslave any other human being.'

The oar master's eyes briefly light up with hope - until he sees the belaying pin swinging down at his head.

'We'll have to beach her,' says the scarred man, wiping a clod of mashed brains off his face. 'With the oars gone we can't rely on the wind.'

The ship runs aground and you and the others split up. Each has his own homeland to try and get back to. 'I never want to see another Gargarean as long as I live,' says one man as he bids you farewell.

You look along the coast. The Sacred Way runs along the shoreline here. Which way will you go?

East goto [**400**](#HeadingNum400)

West goto [**444**](#HeadingNum444)

#### 600

You gather a few things for the journey, wrapping them up in a rag so they will be easier to carry. As you turn back to your meal, a dog is crouching over it.

'You little bastard,' you say, rounding on him.

'Urk,' he says, and immediately vomits green slime all over your bed mat.

You wait, hunger gnawing at your insides. The hours pass but Penthé doesn't come. She sleeps in another room higher upstairs, some even say she even shares the master's bed, and you daren't go looking for her now. As daylight greys the windows you realize that the opportunity for escape has gone.

#### 608

The sinkhole forms a cavernous space, a gouge in the earth filled by a lake or inland sea many kilometres across, around which the Gargareans have built their city. The four great rivers cascade over the lip of the sinkhole, turning into fountains of vapour in their long plunge to the lake far below.

Warrens of streets, many of them with steep steps or perilous cobbled ramps, wind up the sides of the sinkhole connecting arches and buildings that have been hewn out of the living rock. Flakes of snow swirl down out of the overcast sky, turning the pavements slick and treacherous underfoot. The whole scene is like an icy circle of Hades illuminated by oil lanterns that flare and sputter in the clammy air.

The stone is dark and lichen-stained, the atmosphere dank because of the perpetual lacing of mist that hangs over the surface of the lake. Only at midday does the sun shine directly into the sinkhole, and then but weakly and for a brief time. Otherwise the streets are grey and gloomy. No wonder that the souls of the savage Gargareans are likewise.

If you have the codeword **_Quark_** goto [**382**](#HeadingNum382)

If not goto [**263**](#HeadingNum263)

#### 612

The other Amazons quickly finish off the wounded creature. Together you say a prayer to Artemis to carry its spirit into the realm beyond. Then you set to butchering the carcass.

#### 670

A wolf pack has been tracking you at a cautious distance for a day now. To throw them off the scent, you make your way out to an islet in the middle of the river. The current is strong, but the water is shallow enough that by crouching low you can get hold of rocks on the riverbed. Even so it takes you almost an hour to work your way to the islet and you feel as exhausted as if you'd scaled a mountain.

You climb up out of the water and throw yourself flat under the sheltering trees. You can rest here overnight and try for the far bank tomorrow morning. But as you hover at the edge of sleep, the ground stirs under you. Clumps of soil are rolling together, massing into a long hump. With a sucking sound and a waft of decaying leaves, a pile of moss and twigs and leaves pulls itself out of the ground. It has a long snout dripping with mud, river pebbles for eyes, and its back bristles with pine needles.

Seeing you it gives vent to an earthy howl and you smell its loam-breath, dank as a opened grave. And in that instant you know this is Wolfshadow, the demon who is ineluctably pursuing you. He must have possessed the wolf pack, but now that you've eluded them he has extruded himself into the living world with whatever is to hand.

#### 703

You stride in the direction you think leads to the exit, convinced that the cold fresh air of the mountainside is just ahead - until you turn a corner and run into a dead end.

Retracing your steps nervously, you skirt the heart of the labyrinth where you can hear the minotaur muttering and bellowing to itself. Taking another route, you hurry on to another dead end.

This goes on for days. You get steadily weaker. Finally you are crawling on all fours, your tongue rasping and dry, your head swimming with hunger. You have to rest, just for a moment. You roll onto your back and lie devoid of hope as you wait for the wing of Thanatos to cover you.

#### 704

On a whim you allow the fire to die out and sit gazing at the stars. Beyond the dark sharp edges of the pines, the Milky Way is a blaze of celestial fire.

You are aware of a presence behind you. Something is watching in the stillness of the night. You turn, at first seeing nothing but aware of the threat by the tingle of hairs on the back of your neck.

A clot of shadow floats out of the background of darkness. Eyes glitter flatly as they catch the faint starlight. The silence gives way to a low snarl, barely audible at first, that builds as he prowls nearer. It is the demon Wolfshadow. He is close enough now that you could stretch out your arm and touch him. He bares his white fangs to their roots, the snarl growing savage and urgent in his throat, and the visceral sense of his carnivorous malignity makes you shudder.

If you have any of the following: **honey of Hades**, **weasel** **blood**, a **caged canary**, **fresh fish**, a **harpy's egg**, a **centaur's skull**, **venison sausages**, some **strix stew**, a **honey cake**, a **maggoty pie** or a **shrivelled heart** and wish to discard it goto [**820**](#HeadingNum820)

'A young fellow. He came through with another man. Can't remember their names, but the other was a real thug.' She gives a little shiver. 'A bad boy, that one.'

'And that's all you can tell me?'

'I think they said they were heading over to that little valley between Mount Nysa and the place where those dirty girls live.'

You grit your teeth. 'Dirty girls?'

'Oh,' she sniffs. 'You know. Harpies.'

#### 713

The Gargarean troops are disarmed and many of their warships scuttled. You give orders for a Myrmidon military presence to remain in the city to ensure that your enemies never rebuild their terrible warfleet.

Your elation is only marred by the news you receive later that Master Harboros was killed by a stray arrow a short time after the Gargarean generals had formally surrendered. 'We don't know who shot it, excellency,' reports the officer who has come to tell you.

#### 771

It's as if you've strayed out of the hostel and found your way to one of the dingiest cells in the prison pits further round the sinkhole. The walls are slimy with water trickling through the stone, the bed is made of old crates covered with a lice-ridden blanket, and there is a smell midway between urine and fungus mould.

It's as squalid as any room you've ever had to sleep in, but you say nothing as it occurs to you that the slave's own quarters are probably worse. You spend a restless night and wake up itching and stiff.

#### 775

You take one of the bars and put it by your feet, making a great show of rubbing dust over your hands for a better grip. Borgo and the barker watch with confident grins, unaware that while their attention is on your hands they aren't noticing you work the iron collar down the bar with your feet.

Nodding to indicate you are ready, you take up the bar and pretend to struggle. Then you allow an expression of delighted amazement to creep over your face as you twist the bar at right angles. There is a gasp from the audience. Borgo and the barker have lost their broad smiles.

'Now it's Borgo's turn,' says the barker hastily. 'You have to do better than him to win.'

He's reaching for the other bar, but you quickly twist your own bar nearly straight, jam the iron collar over the soft midsection, and hand that to Borgo. In front of the shepherds he can't refuse it. You watch him struggle to dislodge the iron collar, but you've made sure to wedge it firmly in place.

The audience are booing now. Borgo can't stall any longer. He makes a brave attempt to really bend the bar, but his biceps are more fat than muscle. With a grunt he lets the bar fall, still as straight as when you handed it to him, and the barker resentfully pays out your winnings of 20 pyr.

#### 784

The lead actor recites:

'We spread the tables on the greensward ground;

We feed with hunger, and the bowls go round;

When from the mountain-tops, with hideous cry,

And clatt'ring wings, the hungry harpies fly;

They snatch the meat, defiling all they find,

And, parting, leave a loathsome stench behind.'

They pointedly leave the plates on the stage as they are packing up, perhaps in the hope that some of the audience will donate some food. And they do end up with a few loaves of bread.

'Stale as usual,' you overhear one of the actors say as she chews on a slice of bread. 'What I wouldn't give for some wine to wash it down.'

Caught by local militia, you are locked up for a while and fined all the money you have on you. Cross it off your Adventure Sheet. Some of them would like to execute you, but the magistrate stops them, saying, 'That is not a judgement for us to make. It is for the gods to destroy those who see evil as good.'

#### 834

Nothing you do seems to help. Because of his grotesque appearance and small stature, people treat Eso no better than a animal. They talk about him as if he wasn't there, throw him scraps, and generally jeer at him.

'It's all right,' he says sadly. 'Insults only have power if you let them.'

'Surely you find it hurtful?'

'Let me tell you a story. There was a miser who sold everything he had to buy a lump of gold. He buried the gold and went every day to look at the patch of ground. One of his servants noticed his frequent visits to the spot. He dug up the lump of gold and ran off. The miser, on his next visit, found the hole empty and began to wail and tear his hair. A neighbour, seeing him overcome with grief, said, "Don't carry on so. Get a stone and place it in the hole, and imagine that it's the gold still lying there. It will serve the same purpose, because even when the gold was there you didn't make any use of it."'

'What's the moral?'

'Whatever you read into it. For me it's a reminder that pleasure and pain are all in the mind.'

With warm farewells, you go your separate ways.

'Hardly a mystery,' you say. 'Presumably Palanor got wind of the gems being hidden there, unlocked the warehouse late one night, and filched them.'

'Street lamps?' guffaws a passing local. 'No, and we don't have silk cushions for our pigs, neither. You want those new-fangled nonsenses, you best hie yourself off to Iskandria or some fancy place like that.'

Get the codeword **_Quaestor_** if you don't already have it.

Look for tracks goto [**1020**](#HeadingNum1020)

#### 888

The girl's name is Dunamis. She embraces you timidly, saying, 'Being your slave, what should I do but tend upon the hours and times of your desire?'

'Nonsense,' you tell her. 'You are of the Myrmidon race. Submit to no one. The Myrmidons fought for Achilles at Troy. They are nobody's slaves.'

She looks up at you, crying tears of joy. 'Then I am free?'

It dawns on you that in freeing Dunamis from the slaver you have taken on a great responsibility. You can't abandon her here among the Gargareans. She would soon be taken into slavery again, or worse.

You escort her to the border, a journey of many days. At the gates of Vulcan City you bid her farewell. 'Go directly to your temple, and ensure they give you safe passage back to Iskandria.'

'I can never forget what I owe you,' she blurts out. You're not sure she's heard a word you've said, but you wave as she goes through into Vulcan City. She will be safer there than among the Gargareans, at least.

Get the codeword **_Quench_** and goto [**509**](#HeadingNum509)

#### 921

It's only when you are halfway through your task that you feel a prickling of hairs on the back of your neck and you realize they are not stupid at all. They're very smart. They worked their way around the lake so as to come on you unawares, guided only by the sawing sound of your knife on gristle. You look up to see several huge faces looming like ships' prows in the mist.

You leap up, drenched in the blood of your kill, and run as fast as you can. A split second later and they'd have surrounded you. As it is, you have no time to gather all your belongings. The pitch-lined scrape marks on the ledge suggest that he must have launched the ship, but there's no sign of wreckage. As you descend, you look to the sky, where the first stars are coming out in a violet dusk. Could Ancaeus really have sailed into that uncharted ocean?

#### 943

#### 1003

Throughout the morning you accompany the hunter as he stalks cautiously across the plains, avoiding the frozen grass that would crunch underfoot. From time to time he bends down, scratches at the hard ground, even sniffs the earth. Then he straightens, tastes the wind, and points out a new direction. You exchange few words and you're content to let him take the lead. These are his hunting grounds, after all.

Swirls of snow turn after a few hours into a steady flurry. The wind picks up and soon you are pushing your way through a bitingly cold blizzard. Visibility is down to thirty metres and you can hear nothing over the shrill keen of the wind. You begin to feel disoriented by the endless white haze, perhaps even experiencing a sense of _déjŕ vu_.

You turn towards the hunter, intending to say it's time to hunker down till the blizzard is past. He's off to your left, just visible through the driving snow. You're about to call out when a blurry shape rears up and engulfs him, pulling him to the ground.

You're struggling on through the blizzard looking for somewhere to take shelter.

There is a heart-lurching crack and your foot shifts down a centimetre or so. And now you realize that you've wandered out onto a frozen lake. It could give way under you at any moment.

#### 1057

The boat lurches. You head towards the gangway but it is already too late. The supporting branches give way with a deep snapping sound and twigs and leaves flash past. You are thrown back by the impact as the boat hits the water and is spun around in the current.

You clutch at the porthole and pull yourself upright. What you see outside makes no earthly sense. Dark and light spin in a maelstrom of unpinned time. A gust of frigid air is followed in seconds by a hot dusty breeze that makes you choke. You see mist and fire, sand and ice, rock and greenery, as the boat is tossed through gulfs of space. Finally it strikes something immovable and with a groan of old timbers it breaks apart, flinging you into a chopping briny ocean. You drag yourself up onto a lonely stretch of shore and look around.

#### 1061

A pillared temple stands at the crest of the mountain, stark white against the livid purple sky. Deep in the clouds, lightning spits and mutters. Hailstones sting your face and rattle in the rocky gullies.

If Polymnia is your companion and you want her counsel goto [**125**](#HeadingNum125)

If Galatea is here and you want to talk to her goto [**396**](#HeadingNum396)

Otherwise goto [**77**](#HeadingNum77)

#### 1062

At the northernmost tip of the headland, the sea pounds against the rocks and the mist is torn into fleeting tatters by the wind. Here you find an alcove hewn into a rock. The carvings have been rubbed away by centuries of unrelenting weather, but there is still a plinth with a depression in the centre that looks like it must have been intended as an altar. You place the libation bowl on it.

If you have some **pomegranate wine** goto [**255**](#HeadingNum255)

Otherwise you can make an offering of your own blood (goto [**381**](#HeadingNum381)) or return to the road (goto [**927**](#HeadingNum927)).

#### 1063

The Halizon stronghold sits far above the steppes, a mountain fortress of darkly gleaming granite that is accessible only by steep, narrow staircases built at right angles to the mountainside. A traveller needs to be surefooted and steel-nerved to walk up one of these staircases, each only as wide a single person, with a thousand-foot drop on either side.

As you get further up the staircase, the air becomes thinner. You cannot stop to rest as there are stories of people falling asleep and rolling off the side. Trudging on, you see the fortress getting slowly nearer. Now you can make out the jigsaw lines of its construction. The smooth stone blocks of the walls are cut to fit without mortar, and polished until the sunlight slides off them like oil.

At last you are at the gates of the citadel. The sentries look at you with stony expressions, making no attempt to hide their contempt of outsiders.

If you are female goto [**952**](#HeadingNum952)

If not but your Glory is 2 or less goto [**589**](#HeadingNum589)

Otherwise goto [**316**](#HeadingNum316)

#### 1065

Eso comes with you as far as a settlement at the end of the river valley. Smoke curls up from a cluster of small thatched huts.

'Come on, then.'

He hangs back. 'I don't always get a warm welcome. Sometimes they throw things.'

#### 1066

Flinty rocks skitter and tumble down the steep precipices that surround your trail. You are journeying in the western mountain range. To sailors out at sea, it must look as if the gods raised a wall across the world stretching from heaven to earth.

You have no hope of finding your way westward through the maze of passes down to the road, so where now?

Due north goto [**275**](#HeadingNum275)

North-east goto [**998**](#HeadingNum998)

South-east goto [**876**](#HeadingNum876)

A door in the hillside goto [**655**](#HeadingNum655)

#### 1067

'Go away, Fortunatus,' you say in what you're sure is a pitch-perfect impersonation of one of his owners' voices.

There's a mumbled apology on the other side of the door and you hear him retreat down the stairs. Obviously you can't get out that way - you'd risk bumping straight into him - so you have another go at opening the bedroom window.

#### 1069

The shouts of the triumphant mingle with the screams of the dying and the whimpers of the terrified. From all around comes the discordant music of battle: clanging swords, incessant drums, the hiss and thud of arrows, the crack of timbers. Flames lick around a forest of masts; smoke interlaces with the icy mist; the tang of fresh snapped wood combines with the stench of sweat and fear and spilled blood. Ships collide, prows splintering through hulls, grapples tearing into rigging. All is chaos and desperation, the very sustenance of Ares as he breathes and drinks the violent struggles of mortals.

This is the moment of truth. Roll three dice.

score 3-5 goto [**685**](#HeadingNum685)

score 6-18 goto [**713**](#HeadingNum713)

#### 1070

If Galatea is with you, get the codeword **_Quail_**.

Stories of your exploits have spread even to this remote valley. Awed by you, and seeing you treat Eso with respect, the villagers are deferential to him too. He gets up to recount some of his fables and afterwards they fall over each other in their eagerness to offer him gifts and hospitality.

'Come feast in my hut, Master Eso,' insists the headman.

'And then come to the shrine,' says the shaman, 'where the gods will be eager to bless one who they have gifted with such fluency and wit.'

Seeing you packing up to leave, Eso comes over. 'Thank you, my friend. Funny how they don't seem to notice how ugly I am anymore.'

'No,' you laugh. 'They're too busy tugging their forelocks and licking your boots.'

goto [**853**](#HeadingNum853)

#### 1071

'You're going to want this.' Gyges digs a treetrunk-sized finger in his ear and extracts a small object which he drops into your hand. 'Just wipe the wax off.'

You do so and discover a **medallion of Hermes**. Add it to your possessions.

'Anything else?'

'Yeah. Leave the fox.'

'No!' wails the fox. 'He'll eat me.'

'Eat you?' says Gyges. His lips, which resemble two enormous tree roots, split in a rubbery grin. 'Never do that. You're too useful.'

He reaches down and with surprising finesse tweaks a single hair out of the fox's tail.

'Ouch.'

Gyges touches the hair to the edge of one of his axes and it falls in half. 'See? You're the golden goose, my foxy friend. I wouldn't eat you while I need to test my axe blades.'

You leave them to it and head back through the woods.

goto [**363**](#HeadingNum363)

#### 1072

'Stay back,' warns the stranger as you approach. 'I bear a curse.'

'What kind of curse?'

'The worst.' He gives you a wild stare. 'I obtained a blessing at the temple, but there is no one less worthy of the favour of the gods than I. So now I have begun to doubt that the gods are wise, or even that they exist. This crisis of faith is the most terrible curse imaginable.'

'The solution is simple. Transfer the blessing to me.'

All this time he has been twitching nervously, but simple astonishment makes him suddenly calm and collected. 'Of course!'

Gain one blessing if you don't already have the maximum number allowed. As you head on, the stranger calls after you, 'Perhaps you are wiser than the gods. But can a mortal surpass the immortals?'

'Try not to think about it,' you call back.

Head south goto [**1066**](#HeadingNum1066)

Go south-east goto [**998**](#HeadingNum998)

Search for the hippogriffs' eyrie goto [**641**](#HeadingNum641)

#### 1074

Cross off 100 pyr. The two men are only grudgingly mollified. You get the feeling they were just warming up for a good shouting match.

'Can we get along home now?' says the farmer's wife.

'I hope you've got a spare grindstone,' the miller's wife says to her husband.

You can add the **grindstone** you've bought to your possessions.

goto [**984**](#HeadingNum984)

#### 1075

'One mammoth will make mincemeat of us,' you tell them, 'if we just run in and start jabbing at it. So we're going to be smart about this.'

You show them how to dig a line of pits and cover them with interlaced twigs and moss. Then one hunter creeps forward towards a solitary mammoth, throws a spear into its flank that only serves to enrage it, and runs towards where the rest of you are crouched in hiding.

The mammoth blunders into the pit, which is quite shallow but keeps the ponderous beast stuck long enough for you all to shower it with spears. Weakened by blood loss, it rolls onto its side and lies there breathing in ragged gasps. You jump down and finish it off. 'Orion take your spirit, brave one,' you say to it. 'Your death honours us.'

As the leader of the hunt you get the **mammoth hide**. Add it to your possessions. The others each take a parcel of meat almost too big to carry and stagger off back to their separate villages.

goto [**984**](#HeadingNum984)

#### 1076

This is the end. Delete everything on your Adventure Sheet including attributes, codewords, companions, possessions, and so forth. Erase any ticks or other records you have written in boxes throughout all the books.

When you are ready to begin again with a new character goto **1** in any of the Vulcanverse gamebooks.
